    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fbfb1e52-1171-4c56-966d-d31f785c2412'

<span id="freeTextContainer6731961481005704154">The year is 885, and England is at peace, divided between the Danish kingdom to the north and the Saxon kingdom of Wessex in the south. But a dead man has risen, and new Vikings have invad</span>
  <span id="freeText6731961481005704154" style="display:none">The year is 885, and England is at peace, divided between the Danish kingdom to the north and the Saxon kingdom of Wessex in the south. Warrior by instinct and Viking by nature, Uhtred, the dispossessed son of a Northumbrian lord, has land, a wife and children—and a duty to King Alfred to hold the frontier on the Thames. But a dead man has risen, and new Vikings have invaded the decayed Roman city of London with dreams of conquering Wessex... with Uhtred’s help. Suddenly forced to weigh his oath to the king against the dangerous turning tide of shifting allegiances and deadly power struggles, Uhtred—Alfred’s sharpest sword—must now make the choice that will determine England’s future.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1224878875" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1224878875" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1224878875?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=4-star-reads">4-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1224878875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17534108535852701421">Uhtred is in his prime; he has name and reputation, and he also has the youth and energy to complete his goals. He is beyond tried and tested; he is the master of his craft; he is the mighty Uhtred and he is now a war lord to be feared. I pity the man that crosses swords with him. <br/><br/><b> <i> The shield itself, rimmed with iron, was painted with a wolfs head, my badge, and at my left hung serpents breath and at my right Wasp-sting, and I strode towards the gate with the sun rising behind me to throw my lo</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText17534108535852701421" style="display:none">Uhtred is in his prime; he has name and reputation, and he also has the youth and energy to complete his goals. He is beyond tried and tested; he is the master of his craft; he is the mighty Uhtred and he is now a war lord to be feared. I pity the man that crosses swords with him. <br><br><b> <i> The shield itself, rimmed with iron, was painted with a wolfs head, my badge, and at my left hung serpents breath and at my right Wasp-sting, and I strode towards the gate with the sun rising behind me to throw my long shadow on the filth-strewn street. I was a warlord in all my glory, I had come to kill, and no one at the gate knew it." </i></b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456588820i/18254813._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book opens with a gory hanging that is just another necessity of war. Uhtred has learnt that a man must be brutal if his enemies are to fear him; he has learnt that in order to maintain his warrior reputation he must be merciless. Men must fear him or his reputation as a dangerous foe wouldn’t exist. The fear is part of his persona; it is part of his character, and a necessary facet of being a successful general. If his enemies can’t predict his actions or understand the way he conducts his business, then half of the job is done before Uhtred has even drawn his sword. He’s already won. <br><br>It took Uhtred a while to catch on, through serving Alfred he will never receive the deserved glory for the services he has rendered to him. The king is thankless and views Uhtred’s success on the battlefield in a different light. He can never fully trust him or allow him too much power. He fears that his dog may turn round and bite him, which is a shame because for all Uhtred’s savagery he still possesses a degree of honour and loyalty. He quite easily could have been Alfred’s man if he, in turn, treated him with respect. The king has ordered him to be an advisor to his cousin, which means Uhtred will do all the thinking, and all the killing, whilst his weak cousin will get all the rewards. Such is the life of Uhtred. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456589079i/18254834._SY540_.png" width="400" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The familiarity of these novels really gives the series a sense of cohesion. When you pick up the next instalment, there is absolutely no doubt as to what you are going to get: more Uhtred. You’re going to get another chapter of his life; you’re going to get the next stage of his development; you’re going to see the narrative change as he comes closer and closer to the retrospective Uhtred that is telling the tale. Uhtred must bide his time in service to Alfred because one day he will be able to reclaim his family home by himself. It’s only a matter of time. <br><br><u> The Saxon Stories </u><br>1. <i>The Last Kingdom-</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1184243350?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">A fine five stars</a><br>2. <i>The Pale Horsman-</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1186450906?type=review#rating_37274009" rel="nofollow noopener">A brilliant five stars</a><br>3.<i>Lords of the North-</i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1199820612?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">A vengeful four stars</a><br>4.<i>Sword Song- </i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1224878875?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">A familiar four stars</a><br>5.<i>The Burning Land-</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1307749308?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">A loyal five stars</a><br>6.<i> Death of Kings </i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1390733251?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">A mighty five stars</a><br><br>I don’t think I’ll ever get tired of reading this series; I could read twenty books on this character. You’re more than likely to get tired of seeing my reviews of the Saxon Stories before I get tired of reading the series. It will be interesting to see how it all ends. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17534108535852701421" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Athena Shardbearer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4159427-athena-shardbearer"><img alt="Athena Shardbearer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546027968p2/4159427.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1197659190?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Athena Shardbearer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Athena Shardbearer" href="/user/show/4159427-athena-shardbearer">Athena Shardbearer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=lord-markus-the-book-pusher">lord-markus-the-book-pusher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=kinda-want">kinda-want</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=having-book-babies">having-book-babies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1197659190" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer569272118070155804"><br/><i>
  <blockquote>"So long as there is a kingdom on this windswept island, there will be war. So we cannot flinch from war. We cannot hide from its cruelty, its blood, its stench, its vileness or its joy, because war will come to us whether we want it or not. War is fate, and wyrd bið ful ãræd. Fate is inescapable."</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/><br/>The one thing I love most of this series is the beautiful writing. Cornwell has such a way with words, how to twist them together to make these beautiful scenes even when its a horrible killing. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText569272118070155804" style="display:none"><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"So long as there is a kingdom on this windswept island, there will be war. So we cannot flinch from war. We cannot hide from its cruelty, its blood, its stench, its vileness or its joy, because war will come to us whether we want it or not. War is fate, and wyrd bið ful ãræd. Fate is inescapable."</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><br />The one thing I love most of this series is the beautiful writing. Cornwell has such a way with words, how to twist them together to make these beautiful scenes even when its a horrible killing. These warriors are warriors, I want to get up and fight and drink with them! <br /><br />This book was much slower than the last three and I think it has a lot to do with Uhtred growing up....a little. I hate Aethelred, love Aethelflead, Gisela and Alfred is growing on me. I guess I can see reason now with him and all he does.<br /><br />I feel like if I say anymore I will give away more than I want to. There are so many things that have happened that now I think I'm with the Saxons....WHAT...NOT THE VIKINGS????? I know?! But it makes sense...right? <br /><br />I can't wait to get into the next book. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

</blockquote><br>I had a super long review written for this series but I deleted the document accidentally so let me share with you at least some major points to explain my reasons for loving this series so much:<br><br>* Astonishing storytelling skills. Bernard Cornwell brought 9th century England alive for me.<br><br>* Unforgettable narrator. Uhtred of Bebbanburg is unapologetic and ruthless yet lovable and admiration worthy character with brilliant military strategic mind. He is a true hero!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497621564ra/23044089.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>* Complex and fascinating side characters that you will love to come back to.<br><br>* Constant philosophical battle between paganism and Christianity that depicts given period precisely.<br><br>* Well thought-out storyline and twists.<br><br>* War and fight scenes are chillingly realistic. I really felt like I was there with Uhtred, fighting every new enemy or being part of countless shield wars.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463241704ra/19097865.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>All in all, The Warrior Chronicles/Saxon Stories series (all 10 available books) is spectacular story with spectacular writing. It is one of the best historical fiction stories I have ever read and it is the perfect example of how to write engaging historical fiction series that never get boring or predictable!<br><br>Moreover, I loved author’s note at the end of every book where author explained which parts were based on historical facts and which parts of his novel he made up. <br><br>RECOMMENDED!</span>

<div id="review_3283384363" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3283384363" />
    <a title="Amanda Hupe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11658047-amanda-hupe"><img alt="Amanda Hupe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535036536p2/11658047.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3283384363?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda Hupe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda Hupe" href="/user/show/11658047-amanda-hupe">Amanda Hupe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780008164423" href="/book/show/33392360-sword-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11658047-amanda-hupe?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11658047-amanda-hupe?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3283384363" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14545124101684690646">And the adventure continues!! Sword Song by Bernard Cornwell is the 4th book in the Saxon Stories series. As always, this book continues the chronicles of Uhtred of Bebbanburg. The year is 885 and Uhtred has given his oath to Alfred and lives with his wife, Gisela. There is peace but peace is very fragile. There are rumors that a man has come back from the dead and predicts the next king of Mercia. Aethelflaed is the daughter of Alfred and is married to Aethelred of Mercia. When she is kidnapped</span>
  <span id="freeText14545124101684690646" style="display:none">And the adventure continues!! Sword Song by Bernard Cornwell is the 4th book in the Saxon Stories series. As always, this book continues the chronicles of Uhtred of Bebbanburg. The year is 885 and Uhtred has given his oath to Alfred and lives with his wife, Gisela. There is peace but peace is very fragile. There are rumors that a man has come back from the dead and predicts the next king of Mercia. Aethelflaed is the daughter of Alfred and is married to Aethelred of Mercia. When she is kidnapped, Alfred sends Uhtred to bargain for his daughter but also maintain peace…<br /><br />WARNING: POSSIBLE SPOILERS<br /><br />I almost forget where one book begins and the other ends because once I finish one book, I immediately start the next one. I seriously cannot get enough of this story, the history, and the characters. Uhtred is one of the characters who is impossible not to love. He is a fierce warrior, demands justice, and is passionate about honor. In fact, he is always mentioning how he places a sword in his enemy’s hands at their death so they may live in Valhalla. He is also hilarious. He has a quick wit which I just adore.<br /><br />“He still has a removable head…”<br /><br />SWORD SONG<br />Uhtred is the narrator of the story and he is not the only character. As a narrator, he is very perspective. There are many wonderful additional plotlines in this novel. Some that completely broke my heart. I want to live in a world where two particular characters can be together.<br /><br />This book can be read as a standalone, but I do not recommend it. There is so much backstory that helps readers understand the characters and the reasons for the events that have occurred. I recommend that readers begin with book one. Also, if you listen to the audiobooks, you are in for a treat. Jonathon Keeble is one of my favorite narrators! This book gets 5 out of 5 stars!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14545124101684690646" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_387513472" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/387513472" />
    <a title="Nate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6803829-nate"><img alt="Nate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413944642p2/6803829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/387513472?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nate" href="/user/show/6803829-nate">Nate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6803829-nate?shelf=middle-ages">middle-ages</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer387513472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9030160514565845671">Cornwell still hasn't let me down with this series. The villains are still easy to hate and there were even characters I wholly liked (Pyrlig is great.) The relative lack of major events in <i>Lords of the North</i> made it a slower read for me than <i>The Pale Horseman</i>, and although this one seemed still primarily focused on the smaller stories of Uhtred and Æthelflæd there was a ton of action and purposeful movement.<br/><br/>I have to say that I'm proud of Uhtred. A whole 300+ pages and he didn't commit a single</span>
  <span id="freeText9030160514565845671" style="display:none">Cornwell still hasn't let me down with this series. The villains are still easy to hate and there were even characters I wholly liked (Pyrlig is great.) The relative lack of major events in <i>Lords of the North</i> made it a slower read for me than <i>The Pale Horseman</i>, and although this one seemed still primarily focused on the smaller stories of Uhtred and Æthelflæd there was a ton of action and purposeful movement.<br /><br />I have to say that I'm proud of Uhtred. A whole 300+ pages and he didn't commit a single brutal murder of a defenseless person. Either he's getting soft in his old age of twenty-eight or that spark of developing character I saw in the other books is slowly coming to fruition. Either way it definitely makes me like him a lot more and thusly I get a lot more invested in his story and ultimate fate.<br /><br />Cornwell's writing still surprises me with not only its vivid depiction of day-to-day life and war in 10th century Britain but its devotion to describing the beauty and detail of the island. I never thought that I would enjoy in-depth descriptions of estuaries and inlets and that kind of thing but I definitely did while reading this book. He obviously has a strong affection for Britain and it shows with these books.<br /><br />After four books in a row I'm still enjoying them a lot and I'm excited to start the next one but I have to say I'm not sure how Cornwell's going to keep them so entertaining. I enjoy his formula but only because he manages to mix up the situations, characters, areas, etc. within that formula. With each passing book I'm sure this is going to get harder and harder, but he hasn't let me down yet. Onto the next one and I'll see how he pulls it off.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9030160514565845671" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_665347523" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/665347523" />
    <a title="Graham Crawford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5884833-graham-crawford"><img alt="Graham Crawford" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486092333p2/5884833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/665347523?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Graham Crawford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Graham Crawford" href="/user/show/5884833-graham-crawford">Graham Crawford</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer665347523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14252213079174908400">It is a testament to Cornwell's craftsmanship that I enjoy hanging out with Uhtred. I know I should dislike him, he's vain, sullen, petty, often foolish, mostly brutal, and very occasionally, kind. And yet I am fond of him. I grimace when he falls for stupid tricks & when he is vicious without cause. I shake my head and smile when he tries to hide his real motivations from me with low cunning. Uhtred is a very clever, very flawed and very human creation.<br/><br/>So many writers of historical fiction feel</span>
  <span id="freeText14252213079174908400" style="display:none">It is a testament to Cornwell's craftsmanship that I enjoy hanging out with Uhtred. I know I should dislike him, he's vain, sullen, petty, often foolish, mostly brutal, and very occasionally, kind. And yet I am fond of him. I grimace when he falls for stupid tricks &amp; when he is vicious without cause. I shake my head and smile when he tries to hide his real motivations from me with low cunning. Uhtred is a very clever, very flawed and very human creation.<br /><br />So many writers of historical fiction feel the need to modernize their protagonists - all those perky girls who ride astride and hate embroidery, all the bleeding heart liberal heroes who fret over slavery and violence and all the other nasty period habits modern readers find unpalatable. Those sort of books might be populated by nicer folk, but they don't ring true. Uhtred feels like a real Saxon, and though I am fond of him - if I was on fire, he wouldn't piss on me to put it out - He'd probably throw another faggot on and warm his mead.<br /><br />Alfred is probably closest to our modern sensibilities, well maybe a evangelical Christian from the Bible Belt - and seeing him through Uhtred's eyes makes the king much more entertaining as a character. There is a layering &amp; an irony of narrative that makes these books much more complex than they appear.<br /><br />The language is simple, though it does have the rhythm and stress of Anglo Saxon poetry - thankfully without the alliteration, but there are quite complex historical themes at work. Of particular interest in this book is the role of the oath and how Alfred uses this to slowly bind people to him and his notion of an emerging England. The oath of fealty was to become the cornerstone of Feudal control in the Medieval period, and it is fascinating to see the evolution of this type of government through the eyes of a warrior of the old school. You really get a sense of how manipulative Alfred must have been. No matter how hard Uhtred wriggles, he can't escape Alfred's hook - any more than he can escape his Fate.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14252213079174908400" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1264264691?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8118446-sword-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=not-a-bookclub-club">not-a-bookclub-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-male">author-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own-backlog">own-backlog</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1264264691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17458943091256767182"><b>Executive Summary:</b> Another great entry in this series, that seemed to be over before it started. How can you not like Uhtred of Bebbanburg?<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br/>I've never really been a big historical fiction fan before discovering this series. I'm not enough of a history buff to know what elements are true, and which are fictional. Regardless this series continues to be fascinating and engrossing.<br/><br/>Compared to many of the doorstopping fantasy books I tend to read, these feel minuscule by comparison. So </span>
  <span id="freeText17458943091256767182" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> Another great entry in this series, that seemed to be over before it started. How can you not like Uhtred of Bebbanburg?<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />I've never really been a big historical fiction fan before discovering this series. I'm not enough of a history buff to know what elements are true, and which are fictional. Regardless this series continues to be fascinating and engrossing.<br /><br />Compared to many of the doorstopping fantasy books I tend to read, these feel minuscule by comparison. So much happens in so few pages though. I love to see just what crazy thing Uhtred might do next in his quest for glory.<br /><br />However it's not just Uthred that endears this series to me. He's once again surrounded by a great supporting cast of characters. Some I love, some I hate, and then there is Alfred who I love to hate. I've always disliked Alfred, but after this book he became a total piece of shit. I won't say why, but if you read this book and don't agree with that, I'll be shocked.<br /><br />For a "brutish" warrior, Uthred shows a lot more heart and compassion for people in his life than the pious and cunning Alfred, the man who would be king of all England. It makes for a great contrast.<br /><br />I'm already looking forward to the next book in this series. It's going far too quick for my liking though. Before I know it, I'll be out of books to read, and then what will I do? (Well probably read another of the 100 or so unread books I already own, but that's besides the point).</span>
  <a data-text-id="17458943091256767182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_44997082" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/44997082" />
    <a title="Terri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1968826-terri"><img alt="Terri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356560426p2/1968826.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/44997082?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terri" href="/user/show/1968826-terri">Terri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1968826-terri?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1968826-terri?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer44997082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8281315475938088832">How frustrating. After all the glowing reviews I have left on goodreads for the other books in this Saxon series (the books that precede Swordsong), I find myself in a painfully awkward situation. <br/>I had a genuine love-hate relationship..wait!...love-hate is too strong..let's go with...like-dislike....so, I had a genuine like-dislike relationship with this book. I liked it, yes indeed, but I didn't like all of it and I didn't always like the way it made me feel. I want to try and expound on this,</span>
  <span id="freeText8281315475938088832" style="display:none">How frustrating. After all the glowing reviews I have left on goodreads for the other books in this Saxon series (the books that precede Swordsong), I find myself in a painfully awkward situation. <br />I had a genuine love-hate relationship..wait!...love-hate is too strong..let's go with...like-dislike....so, I had a genuine like-dislike relationship with this book. I liked it, yes indeed, but I didn't like all of it and I didn't always like the way it made me feel. I want to try and expound on this, but it is kind of against my grain to say anything negative about the Saxon series, however (yes, there is a however), I have never been scared of going against the grain, so let's rush on.<br />I have read another reviewer of this series on goodreads who mentions the anti-Christian sentiment that Bernard Cornwell imparts upon Uhtred's tale. I didn't really feel it most strongly until this book and it was actually so unpleasant in Swordsong that I found myself loathing characters too much. As a reader, this puts you on dangerous ground...or should I say it puts the writer on 'a slippery slope'? If a writer makes his characters too abhorrent, it is certainly a slippery slope and they will lose favour with his or her readers. In Cornwell's case, he creates a plethora of abhorrent characters and then flogs you over the head with them for page after page. <br />Most of these loathsome characters are religious zealots, monks, priests and overtly religious, annoying, incompetent, asinine nobles and rulers. Alfred is painful to read about, but he always has been. Now you have his new son in law who is ten times more excruciating to read about. Add in every unsavoury, slimy, irritating religious character that has ever appeared individually in the Saxon series to date, and you have yourself a big pot of steaming, religious zealot stew served up over 400 or so pages. Mmmmmmmm......a tempting concoction? No, I don't think so.<br />Usually, these loathsome creatures take a backseat position in the Saxon series and while they do annoy me in all the other books, it is because of that backseat position and a limited presence, that I have been able to tolerate them and still love the books. This time, ah, not so much.<br />But hateful characters were not my only problem with Swordsong (I wish that it were the only one).<br />Uhtred has become a subdued, old married man with kids. I miss the old Uhtred and hope for him to return in The Burning Land. I like the character written in as his wife, but having him find love and marriage and kids has also resulted in Uhtred becoming a respectable, dull husband and father.<br />Now, after reading back through my review here so far, I hear you wondering about what it is I exactly I liked about Swordsong, after all, did I not say I had a 'like' -dislike relationship with it?<br />And I did not lie, I did like half of this book also. The last half. More of the trademark brutality, more of the Danes and Uhtred's interaction with them. And he always interacts well with the Danes. <br /> Uhtred gets out from underneath the skirts of his wife, and the skirts of Alfred's robes, and remembers that he is a warrior capable of great warrior things. That is the Uhtred I love to read about.<br />Still, despite liking the last half of this book, I didn't love it enough to go straight into The Burning Land. I had to have a break from these horrid, hateful characters that make my skin crawl.<br />I decided to read Julian Rathbone's The Last English King instead. Once I have finished this, and distanced myself from the Saxon series for a spell, then I might be better prepared for dealing with Bernard's more repugnant characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8281315475938088832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1646671993" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1646671993" />
    <a title="Veronica " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7035111-veronica"><img alt="Veronica " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360466651p2/7035111.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1646671993?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronica " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronica " href="/user/show/7035111-veronica">Veronica </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061379741" href="/book/show/4009500-sword-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7035111-veronica?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1646671993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16114348303438046758"><b>**Re-read in April 2019: I'd forgotten the plot of this book so it was almost like my first time through. I like older Uhtred much better than his younger, more brash self. This is also marks where I left off with the series so from here on out all the books will be fresh and new to me. Still four stars.</b><br/><br/>Sword Song is the fourth in Cornwell's Saxon Tales series and it picks up the threads of Uhtred's life roughly eight years after the events of the last book. Those eight years have seen a tentati</span>
  <span id="freeText16114348303438046758" style="display:none"><b>**Re-read in April 2019: I'd forgotten the plot of this book so it was almost like my first time through. I like older Uhtred much better than his younger, more brash self. This is also marks where I left off with the series so from here on out all the books will be fresh and new to me. Still four stars.</b><br /><br />Sword Song is the fourth in Cornwell's Saxon Tales series and it picks up the threads of Uhtred's life roughly eight years after the events of the last book. Those eight years have seen a tentative peace settle between the countries of Wessex, East Anglia, and Mercia. King Alfred of Wessex, his end goal of a unified England ever in his mind, has been working on shoring up the defenses in Wessex and has tasked Uhtred with a part in making a more secure Wessex a reality. But new players have arrived and new alliances are threatening the fragile, political status quo and Uhtred is once again the linch pin on which the fate of England hangs. <br /><br />It's been awhile since I read the previous book in this series and I wish I had taken better notes on the different characters because I had some difficulty recalling just who everyone was in relation to Uhtred and Cornwell doesn't spend a lot of time or energy in rehashing old information. After I settled into the story however, things started to come back to me and once again I was swept up in the action. It's a well paced story and it's a sign of the quality of the writing and the storytelling that I can be so wrapped up in it despite the fact that I don't always like the main protagonist or the choices he makes. But Uhtred is now 28 years old and is showing signs that he's not the same, hot tempered youth he once was. Oh he's still arrogant, to be sure, a pagan surrounded by Christians, but he's less inclined to be as reactionary as he once was and that's been a welcome change in my opinion. His home life has settled into domestic contentment but that hasn't dulled his skill in battle and despite the fact that he and Alfred don't like each other, like...at all, they nevertheless respect the skills of the other.<br /><br />As with the previous books, Sword Song presents a political chessboard, this time with the city of Lundene (eventually to become London) threatened with checkmate. Reading about all the political maneuverings and the battle strategizing makes this another page turner and no one writes a battle sequence quite like Cornwell.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16114348303438046758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2383923155" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/155663-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581956036p2/155663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2383923155?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/155663-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/155663-david?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2383923155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4656955022533804202">This fourth book in the Saxon Stories by Bernard Cornwell is marvelous! It countinues the same story of Uhtred of Beppenburg, who was born a Saxon in the ninth century. Uhtred has dual loyalties to the Saxons and to the Danes. He is pledged to King Alfred, but he loves the Danes and their warrior attitude toward life. This dual-philosophy gives the stories added drama and interest. <br/><br/>I wholeheartedly recommend the series; but I have not been reading the books--I have been listening to them. This b</span>
  <span id="freeText4656955022533804202" style="display:none">This fourth book in the Saxon Stories by Bernard Cornwell is marvelous! It countinues the same story of Uhtred of Beppenburg, who was born a Saxon in the ninth century. Uhtred has dual loyalties to the Saxons and to the Danes. He is pledged to King Alfred, but he loves the Danes and their warrior attitude toward life. This dual-philosophy gives the stories added drama and interest. <br /><br />I wholeheartedly recommend the series; but I have not been reading the books--I have been listening to them. This book is read by Jonathan Keeble, who does a fantastic narration. He is older than the narrator of the earlier books (Tom Sellwood). This is appropriate, because it becomes clear in this book that the writer (it is all in the first person) is an old man, telling the story of his life. Keeble's reading, coupled with Cornwell's gripping telling of the battle scenes and Uhtred's torn allegiances, make the audiobook a phenomenal experience.<br /><br />I also recently watched "The Last Kingdom", which is an excellent TV series that is based on the books. Up until now, the TV series was pretty true to the novels. But the TV series departs significantly from this fourth book in the series; there isn't really a battle for London at all. This was probably a shortcut to get through the story more expeditiously; the TV series is good, but different.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4656955022533804202" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2321744029" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2321744029" />
    <a title="Donna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13244359-donna"><img alt="Donna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396758075p2/13244359.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2321744029?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna" href="/user/show/13244359-donna">Donna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13244359-donna?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2321744029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7287637168717441809">This one gets 4 stars instead of 5 for only one reason: its an 'audiobook thing'. They changed narrators and although this narrator had an excellent voice, it wasn't Uhtred's voice. The new narrator sounded way too old. Once I could separate the voice from the story, I was just fine.<br/><br/>I am enjoying this series. It has been a solid 4 - 5 star series for me. I love the way the author has developed the characters, and some of them are quite complicated....like Uhtred. He has a love-hate relationship </span>
  <span id="freeText7287637168717441809" style="display:none">This one gets 4 stars instead of 5 for only one reason: its an 'audiobook thing'. They changed narrators and although this narrator had an excellent voice, it wasn't Uhtred's voice. The new narrator sounded way too old. Once I could separate the voice from the story, I was just fine.<br /><br />I am enjoying this series. It has been a solid 4 - 5 star series for me. I love the way the author has developed the characters, and some of them are quite complicated....like Uhtred. He has a love-hate relationship with almost everything around him and with everyone in his life and yet it works. And best of all, it never sounds overworked. I now need to get my hands on the rest of the books or audiobooks.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7287637168717441809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1160702453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1160702453" />
    <a title="Georgina Ortiz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7387625-georgina-ortiz"><img alt="Georgina Ortiz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327892842p2/7387625.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1160702453?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Georgina Ortiz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Georgina Ortiz" href="/user/show/7387625-georgina-ortiz">Georgina Ortiz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1160702453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5175970762524350601">There are so many things to like about Mr. Cornwell's "Sword Song," but what stood out for me was (decidedly "pagan" and Thor devotee) Uthred's unlikely friendship with two priests: the fierce Welsh warrior Father Pyrlig and King Alfred's adviser and scholar Father Beocca.<br/><br/><i>Uhtred on choosing Father Pyrlig:</i><br/>"On one side a kingdom, Viking friends and wealth, and on the other a Briton who was the priest of a religion that sucks joy from this world like dusk swallowing daylight. Yet I did not think. I</span>
  <span id="freeText5175970762524350601" style="display:none">There are so many things to like about Mr. Cornwell's "Sword Song," but what stood out for me was (decidedly "pagan" and Thor devotee) Uthred's unlikely friendship with two priests: the fierce Welsh warrior Father Pyrlig and King Alfred's adviser and scholar Father Beocca.<br /><br /><i>Uhtred on choosing Father Pyrlig:</i><br />"On one side a kingdom, Viking friends and wealth, and on the other a Briton who was the priest of a religion that sucks joy from this world like dusk swallowing daylight. Yet I did not think. I chose, or fate chose, and I chose friendship. Pyrlig was my friend."<br /><br /><i>Uhtred on Father Beocca:</i><br />"He had a club foot, a squint, and a palsied left hand. He was blind in his wandering eye that had gone as white as his hair, for he was now nearly fifty years old. Children jeered at him in the streets and some folk made the sign of the cross, believing that ugliness was a mark of the devil, but he was as good a Christian as any I have ever known."<br /><br /><i>Funny repartees involving Uhtred and Beocca...</i><br />"Too many people were talking in the church!" Beocca complained. "This was a holy day, Uhtred, a sacred day, a celebration of the sacrament, and people were talking as if they were at market!"<br />"I was one of them," I (Uhtred) said.<br />"You were?" he asked, squinting up at me. "Well, you shouldn't have been talking. It's just plain bad manners! And insulting to God! I'm astonished at you, Uhtred, I really am! I'm astonished and disappointed."<br />"Yes, father," I said, smiling.<br /><br /><i>...and Uhtred and Pyrlig:</i><br />"But I've known Aethelflaed forever!" I exclaimed.<br />"He fears you know her only too well," Pyrlig said, "and it drives him to madness."<br />"But that's stupid!" I spoke angrily.<br />"It's jealousy," Pyrlig said, "and all jealousy is stupid." <br /><br /><br /><b>More favorite passages from the book:</b><br /><br />"It is strange what men talk about before battle. Anything except what faces them. I have stood in a shield wall, staring at an enemy bright with blades and dark with menace, and heard two of my men argue furiously about which tavern brewed the best ale. Fear hovers in the air like a cloud and we talk of nothing to pretend that the cloud is not there." —Uhtred, p.10<br /><br />"You never, ever, tell others of your crimes, not unless they are so big as to be incapable of concealment, and then you describe them as policy or statecraft." —Uhtred, p.36<br /><br />"Yet I was sworn to Alfred. I was sworn to defend Wessex. I had given Alfred my oath and without oaths we are no better than beasts." —Uhtred, p.55<br /><br />"Cowardice is always with us, and bravery, the thing that provokes the poets to make songs about us, is merely the will to overcome the fear." —Uthred, p.136<br /><br />"You live by obeying the rules. You make a reputation, boy, by breaking them." —Uhtred, p.149<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5175970762524350601" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_115714249" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115714249" />
    <a title="Steve " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4121048-steve"><img alt="Steve " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395963300p2/4121048.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115714249?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve " href="/user/show/4121048-steve">Steve </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4121048-steve?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115714249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5976207364278817502">An absolutely fascinating era in English history; one where the tides could so easily have turned and left England as Daneland. The historical place names and character names are pretty much real and add to the whole feel of the 9th century. Where a sickly, extremely pious, but sharp witted prince becomes not only a king, when he was not directly in line to take the throne. But becomes known as King Alfred The Great, despite his frail body and constant illness, and despite (or maybe, because of)</span>
  <span id="freeText5976207364278817502" style="display:none">An absolutely fascinating era in English history; one where the tides could so easily have turned and left England as Daneland. The historical place names and character names are pretty much real and add to the whole feel of the 9th century. Where a sickly, extremely pious, but sharp witted prince becomes not only a king, when he was not directly in line to take the throne. But becomes known as King Alfred The Great, despite his frail body and constant illness, and despite (or maybe, because of) his pious beliefs and surrounding himself with some dubious priests. <br /><br />But, Alfred needs warriors, he needs armies, he needs a Warlord that men will follow because he fights at their side and slaughters his enemies. It turns out that Lord Uhtred, a saxon born Lord, raised by the very pagans that Alfred needs destroyed, is the only man for the task. But, someone who is so renowned as a battle lord who also has a Lord's rights to land in the north of England, needs to be kept on a short leash. And Lord Uhtred, although loyal, is not a man to be tethered or dictated to. <br /><br />Lord Uhtred of Bebbanburg is a brilliant character, well written and certainly well thought out. This book, and the Saxon series as a whole, has no shortage of really well written characters. Diversity, amnity, and alliegence are done with skill in the main and supporting characters. <br /><br />The real bonding between Lord Uhtred and Lady AEthelflaed (King Alfred's daughter, married to a cowardly, abusive ass) is just starting to bloom in this book. Uhtred's old adversary Jarl Haesten is a slimey piece of work. And the two brothers Jarl's Sigefrid and Erik couldn't be much more diverse. Jarl Erik actually comes across as a decent man. There is a point, after one of the battles where Erik and his brother are retreating, where Erik asks who leads. One of Uhtred's friends, the warrior priest, Pyrlig, points out that Lord AEthelred (the abusive husband to King Alfred's daughter) commands, and Lord Uhtred disobeys. Lord Uhtred then gives Jarl Erik, and his men, their freedom. <br /><br />There is so much more to this book. And I believe it to be one of the best three in the Saxon series, so far. I await the next ;) </span>
  <a data-text-id="5976207364278817502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6736730895332269362">I have truly loved every book in this series, but I think that this one was my favorite so far. Again, I won't go into too much detail for fear of spoilers, but I have definitely grown attached to this cast of characters.   <span id="freeText6736730895332269362" style="display:none">I have truly loved every book in this series, but I think that this one was my favorite so far. Again, I won't go into too much detail for fear of spoilers, but I have definitely grown attached to this cast of characters. I have enjoyed their journey (and in particular, Uhtred's journey) all along, but I think that this installment has a plot that I was able to get lost in more than the last book. Not to mention, the writing was some of Cornwell's best, in my opinion. I can't count the number of times I found myself pausing &amp; rereading passages just because they were so beautiful. Once again, I loved it, simply put. I'm having such a wonderful time with this series, especially getting to read it with my hubby! </span>

<div id="review_361483231" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/361483231" />
    <a title="Billy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10554432-billy"><img alt="Billy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591121312p2/10554432.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/361483231?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Billy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Billy" href="/user/show/10554432-billy">Billy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10554432-billy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer361483231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1321952745834135695">Uhtred is one of the GREATEST literary figures ever created!, <br/><br/>The Saxon Chronicles, panned from the outset as Cornwell trying to return to his British roots, has proven to be a juggernaut that cannot be stopped by bad and, in this case, off-base, press reviews.<br/><br/>Book 4, 'Sword Song: The Battle for London', continues the story of Lord Uhtred, Saxon born, Dane raised, sworn man of King Alfred the great. In this installment, Uhtred fights to take London back from the invading Northemen, the Vikings. </span>
  <span id="freeText1321952745834135695" style="display:none">Uhtred is one of the GREATEST literary figures ever created!, <br /><br />The Saxon Chronicles, panned from the outset as Cornwell trying to return to his British roots, has proven to be a juggernaut that cannot be stopped by bad and, in this case, off-base, press reviews.<br /><br />Book 4, 'Sword Song: The Battle for London', continues the story of Lord Uhtred, Saxon born, Dane raised, sworn man of King Alfred the great. In this installment, Uhtred fights to take London back from the invading Northemen, the Vikings. Uhtred, who loves the Vikings far more than he cares for the Christian religion of the king he is continually sworn to serve, now must fight to take back London and to save Alfred, and his family, from defeat at the hands of the Norse invaders.<br /><br />This book, beginning in the year 885, probably doesn't see the end of 886 before the final page is turned. Unlike the first 3 offerings in this series, this book covers a very short period of time, perhaps 6-8 months. It is a fast moving, blood-letting adventure as Uhtred overtakes Danish controlled London whilst his estranged cousin, Aethelred, marries King Alfred's daughter, Aethelflaed, in search of a kingdom of his own. Uhtred is ordered to produce that kingdom as a gift to the newly married couple. Aetheflaed, a young woman whom Uhtred has known and loved as a daughter since she was a child, marries Uhtred's cousin, Aethelred, a man who Uhtred respects little and whom Uhtred, thanks to Alfred's order, owes much; begining with the city of London.<br /><br />As we again hear Uhtred continue the story of his service to Alfred (All of the books in this series are told in first person), we find that a dead Dane skald (poet) is rising from his grave and announcing that Uhtred is to be King of Mercia. Uhtred witnesses this dead rising and follows the corpses instruction to meet with the Danish attackers who want to take the Saxon lands, present day England. Uhtred obeys the skald and travels to the Danish stronghold in London to meet 2 brothers, Erik and Sigefrid Thirgilson, and Haesten, a man who Uhtred once saved and who owed Uhtred an oath, which had been broken. Uhtred, if nothing else, is a man of his word, but he is tempted by the prophecy of the dead skald. He was tempted by the opportunity to fight along side the Northmen that he loved. He was desirous of seeing Alfred dethroned for he hated the pious nature of the king.<br /><br />Thus begins our journey with Uhtred. A journey that will lead to the battle for London, another war with the Danes, and a twist of fate (as Uhtred repeats throughout the book, 'Fate is inexorable') that will test Uhtred's oath like no other test has in his past.<br /><br />Uhtred is one of the greatest characters ever written. He was born a Saxon and rightfully the Lord of Bebbanburg, a county in Northumbria, a part of Saxon England. That birthright was stolen from him by his treacherous uncle earlier in the series. Uhtred longs to regain his birthright but, being a man of his word, he continues to fight for Alfred, and continually waits for his opportunity to return to Bebbanburg and avenge the loss of his birthright.<br /><br />This book, unlike 'Lords of the North', returns to the gory battle and grisly action of the first 2 installments. 'Lords' was as excellent as the other books in this series, but it lacked the battles and the carnage of the first 2 books and this latest installment; 'Lords' was still an excellent book and I recommend that each be read to truly appreciate and understand Uhtred's story.<br /><br />Thankfully, the end of this book is not the end of Uhtred's tale. Cornwell has promised more works about the displaced warrior. With all hope, I can only wait for the Saxon Chronicles to grow to a library the size of which Cornwell has grown his 'Sharpe' series. A continued focus on this man and his adventures in establishing England for Alfred is deserving of at least a large fraction of the number of books produced on Sharpe.<br /><br />If fate is inexorable, I hope against hope that Cornwell will be fated to continue to write Uhtred's tale for many years to come. There is no greater fictional warrior that I can think of that is deserving of a library of books.<br /><br />If you have read the first three books of this series, buy this immediately. If you haven't read the Saxon Chronicles, I strongly recommend that you start from the beginning (The Last Kingdom, The Pale Horseman and Lords of the North) and read all of the books in this series. Cornwell is the master of historical fiction and, with this latest installment, has proven that he continues to excel. But, as great as this book is, don't skip to book 4; read the entire series. I demand that you read the entire series!<br /><br />Highly recommended to anyone that enjoys Viking, Anglo-Saxon, or medieval/dark ages history or historical fiction.<br /><br />THIS ENTIRE SERIES IS PHENOMENAL!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1321952745834135695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_12037571" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/12037571" />
    <a title="Alex Telander" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/595788-alex-telander"><img alt="Alex Telander" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503597052p2/595788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/12037571?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex Telander" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex Telander" href="/user/show/595788-alex-telander">Alex Telander</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/595788-alex-telander?shelf=books-read-in-2008">books-read-in-2008</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer12037571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer695206183437847232">SWORD SONG: THE BATTLE FOR LONDON BY BERNARD CORNWELL: We last left Uhtred, in Lords of the North, apparently an ally with King Alfred, while the Vikings were making a very successful takeover of England, making it seem like there was little hope left for Alfred and his Saxon people. But Alfred has God on his side, and feels he will be ultimately victorious; Uhtred on the other hand, a pagan, cares little for this Christian religion, but is still a little unsure of where his allegiances lie. <br/><br/>Whi</span>
  <span id="freeText695206183437847232" style="display:none">SWORD SONG: THE BATTLE FOR LONDON BY BERNARD CORNWELL: We last left Uhtred, in Lords of the North, apparently an ally with King Alfred, while the Vikings were making a very successful takeover of England, making it seem like there was little hope left for Alfred and his Saxon people. But Alfred has God on his side, and feels he will be ultimately victorious; Uhtred on the other hand, a pagan, cares little for this Christian religion, but is still a little unsure of where his allegiances lie. <br /><br />While the first three of the Saxon Chronicles gave little hope and direction for Uhtred, in Sword Song, he has more to fight for with a wife and child, and another baby on the way. The old Roman town of London, an important one with its link to the Thames, has been taken over by the Vikings. If Alfred gives them London, Wessex is next and soon there will be little left to defend and England will be a Viking nation. So Alfred charges Uhtred with this great task to use the Saxon army, as well as his own loyal men, and take back London.<br /><br />At this point Uhtred is an warrior and a great leader in a shield wall. But with the siege of London, he must mount an attack from the Thames, using ships and men. It will involve all his previous experience of battle, as well as appeasing both the Saxon army, and his own Northmen. His plan is to appear as an ally to the Vikings upon reaching London which, with his history, is a possibility, but then to spring the trap and take back the pivotal town. The question is whether Uhtred will live up to his side of the bargain, with his loyalty being challenged. Coupled with this is Aethelflæd, Alfred’s daughter, who has been recently kidnapped and is being held somewhere in London by a Viking lord; her life must be protected at all costs.<br /><br />Sword Song jumps the bestselling series one big step forward, with this pivotal battle in the creation of the nation of England and its people. Ending on a cliffhanger, Cornwell skillfully leaves fans having to wait another whole year until they can get the next important chapter in the story of Alfred the Great. <br /><br />For more book reviews and exclusive author interviews, go to <a href="http://www.bookbanter.net" rel="nofollow noopener">BookBanter</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="695206183437847232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5880552-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493644616p2/5880552.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/747070543?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha" href="/user/show/5880552-samantha">Samantha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5880552-samantha?shelf=more-historical-than-fiction">more-historical-than-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5880552-samantha?shelf=own-it">own-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5880552-samantha?shelf=saxon-england">saxon-england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5880552-samantha?shelf=british-history">british-history</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer747070543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17547123274245572552">In this fourth installment in the Saxon Warriors series, we find Uhtred continuing to struggle with his loyalties, faith, and destiny. While he feels more of a connection to the Norsemen, he remains paired with Alfred for inexplicable reasons. Uhtred is a mystery wrapped in an enigma, and he is a cruel one. Or, as my husband's short review summed up once I convinced him to read the first few books in the series, "Uhtred is kind of a jerk."<br/> <br/>I still found myself amused by Uhtred's witty irreverenc</span>
  <span id="freeText17547123274245572552" style="display:none">In this fourth installment in the Saxon Warriors series, we find Uhtred continuing to struggle with his loyalties, faith, and destiny. While he feels more of a connection to the Norsemen, he remains paired with Alfred for inexplicable reasons. Uhtred is a mystery wrapped in an enigma, and he is a cruel one. Or, as my husband's short review summed up once I convinced him to read the first few books in the series, "Uhtred is kind of a jerk."<br /> <br />I still found myself amused by Uhtred's witty irreverence, and battle scenes were as vivid and gory as ever. However, I found the ongoing fighting seemed pointless and knocks on Christians wore a little on my nerves. I also didn't need to be reminded every time his name was mentioned that Guthred's Christian name was King Aethelstan. I blame <a href="http://pillingswritingcorner.blogspot.com/2015/04/uhtred-schmutred.html" rel="nofollow noopener">David Pilling's Uhtred Shmutred post</a> for taking some of the fun out of Uhtred's alpha male style.<br /> <br />Uhtred's adventures were certainly still enjoyable and fast paced, but I found that I began looking for him to form more of an objective than dying with a sword in his hand. Uhtred fights alongside the loyal Finan, who shared Uhtred's time in slavery. They fight anyone Alfred tells them to and a few that he doesn't. Not every battle is met with complete success, so there is still some suspense, and the plot is left ripe for the next episode.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17547123274245572552" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer849212801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10949895986785193945">rating: 5.5/5<br/><br/>Ah, Cornwell, you did it yet again. Love, love, love this series!<br/><br/>Uhtred is a little less, uh, murderous in this one (which only means he doesn't kill unarmed -priests- in cold blood). It still has the humor brutality of war, vivid descriptions of life, Uhtred's spontaneous actions, and some new wonderful (and easily hated villainous) characters. A solid novel, highly enjoyable, that had me loving every single word.<br/><br/>And then *bam*, Cornwell actually managed to surprise me with a plot </span>
  <span id="freeText10949895986785193945" style="display:none">rating: 5.5/5<br /><br />Ah, Cornwell, you did it yet again. Love, love, love this series!<br /><br />Uhtred is a little less, uh, murderous in this one (which only means he doesn't kill unarmed -priests- in cold blood). It still has the humor brutality of war, vivid descriptions of life, Uhtred's spontaneous actions, and some new wonderful (and easily hated villainous) characters. A solid novel, highly enjoyable, that had me loving every single word.<br /><br />And then *bam*, Cornwell actually managed to surprise me with a plot twist I didn't see coming. I should have seen it, the hints were all there but I was lulled to semi-predictability through the last three novels and then he goes and throws something like that in. I can't not love it! <br /><br />The ending had me in tears while cursing and yelling at the book. Fortunately it didn't respond (I'd be a bit worried at that). I am still baffled that Cornwell had the ability to shock me with a major plot twist despite his mostly formulaic writing. This was also probably my favorite ending to the Saxon Stories novels so far. It was bittersweet, emotional, but not as wrenching and soul crushing like the second one (that killed one of my favorite characters). <br /><br />This is another strong novel is a series definitely worth reading if you like sword battles, storming fortresses/castles/cities, mocking of Christians by a pagan, and general warrior brutality in a humorous package right out of the late 800s. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10949895986785193945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13413456381312094924">4.5 stars. I still love Uhtred and I even wonder if I'll ever get enough of him. I love seeing how England is slowly being built and Mr Cornwell is a master story-teller.<br/><br/>My only complaint is that I'm starting to see a recurent pattern in the books (hence the 4.5 stars instead of 5) : Uhtred, whose biggest dream is to have his fortress and lands back, keeps giving unwilling oaths to king Alfred (because there's always a good reason) and keeps fighting for him against the Danes (among whom Uhtred </span>
  <span id="freeText13413456381312094924" style="display:none">4.5 stars. I still love Uhtred and I even wonder if I'll ever get enough of him. I love seeing how England is slowly being built and Mr Cornwell is a master story-teller.<br /><br />My only complaint is that I'm starting to see a recurent pattern in the books (hence the 4.5 stars instead of 5) : Uhtred, whose biggest dream is to have his fortress and lands back, keeps giving unwilling oaths to king Alfred (because there's always a good reason) and keeps fighting for him against the Danes (among whom Uhtred was raised and whom he loves), who always outnumber the saxons at first but who keep being defeated in the end, thanks to Uhtred. The same Uhtred who never receive thanks from the ungrateful king Alfred for repeatedly saving the day.<br /><br />Anyway. The story is fascinating. I love history. Bernard Cromwell has simply reminded me how much I do.</span>
